Congratulations! You have won the 1970 United States Senate election in Texas.


As you sit on your sofa with your family around you, waiting for the election results to come in, a sense of dread overcomes you. Did you make the right decisions? Were you too liberal or too conservative? This thought haunts you, but the answer arrives right away from the TV. The News Reporter first goes through the rest of the states in the 1970 midterms before he finally reaches Texas. In one short sentence, he announced to the state of Texas and its 11 million residents that you have won. As you look at the map, you don’t say anything. No one in the room does. Dead silence. You’re stunned. There’s no way. No fricking way.

You snap out of it when your daughter Dorothy shakes you. Then all of the emotions hit everyone. In an instance, the room turned from silence to jubilation. You are overcome by a sense of triumph. You did it, you conquered the democratic machine and broke it apart. You’re now the leader of a Republican movement. One that will conquer the south and transform them like nearly a century ago. You’re in shock, your muscles feel weak and you can’t even move from your sofa. You turn to your family. Barbara notices you and asks if you’re okay. You tell her everything’s alright and she kisses you on the cheeks. George and Jeb celebrate like a bunch of frat boys, jumping up and down as if they just won the Super Bowl. George runs up to you, shaking you while yelling about your victory. You just flash a smile and hug him. No more Loser Bush or Little Shrub, now it’s time for Poppy to be the one in charge.

At Bentsen’s concession speech the next day, he appears late, visibly tired and disheveled. He looks like he aged 10 years before going to the podium. He tries to start his speech but boos and jeering start overwhelming him. He looks up to see a sizable group of Yarborough and liberal supporters headed by none other than Yarborough himself, start telling him to get off the stage. He tries to speak louder than them but his voice is too exhausted, his energy too weak. He cuts it short when they start throwing stuff like marshmallows and campaign pins at him before retreating, probably not wanting to show his face to a single democrat ever again.
